## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials constitutive modeling (thermo-mechanical stress–strain relations)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for thermo-mechanical constitutive laws in materials science (elasticity, plasticity, and temperature-dependent stiffness/strength). Likely relationships include elastic response with temperature-dependent modulus, thermal softening, and nonlinear hardening in strain.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (1D linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime, modulus c0)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (thermoelastic stiffness changes with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening/stiffening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (strong temperature sensitivity of stiffness)
- Thermoelastic with polynomial nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (curved modulus–temperature trend)
- Nonlinear elastic (Landau-type expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (finite-strain/nonlinear elasticity surrogate)
- Nonlinear elastic with temperature-dependent coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (temperature-dependent anharmonicity)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type stress–strain (implicit-like explicit surrogate): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + Abs(epsilon)) + c2 * epsilon (captures transition from high compliance to linear hardening)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (plastic-like hardening in strain with temperature sensitivity)
- Johnson–Cook-like (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (strain hardening times thermal softening/stiffening factor)
- Voce-type saturation hardening surrogate: sigma = c0 + c1 * (c2 + c3 * exp(c4 * epsilon)) (approaches a saturation stress with increasing strain)
- Yield-like transition via smooth switch: sigma = (c0 * epsilon) * (c1 + c2 * tanh(c3 * (Abs(epsilon) - c4))) (elastic-to-plastic transition around a characteristic strain)
- Thermal activation-style softening in strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) / (c3 + exp(c4 * T)) (strength decreases rapidly with temperature rise)
- Coupled polynomial in strain and temperature: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T + c4 * epsilon**2 (generic thermo-mechanical coupling / fitting form)
- Logarithmic strain hardening surrogate (empirical metal hardening): sigma = c0 + c1 * log(c2 + Abs(epsilon)) + c3 * T (slow hardening vs strain with thermal shift)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; temperature dependence often enters as a multiplicative modulus factor like E(T) * epsilon.
- Thermal softening of stiffness/strength → decreasing prefactor with T, commonly via exp(c*T), 1/(c + exp(c*T)), or low-order polynomials in T.
- Strain hardening → sigma grows faster than linear in Abs(epsilon), often captured by epsilon**n with n > 1 or by log(c+Abs(epsilon)) for slow hardening.
- Saturation of hardening at large strain → exponential-in-epsilon terms approaching an asymptote (Voce-type behavior).
- Elastic-to-plastic transition (yielding) → smooth switching functions in strain (tanh or rational blending) that change slope around a characteristic Abs(epsilon).
- T–epsilon coupling → cross-term epsilon*T or temperature-dependent coefficients on epsilon, epsilon**2, epsilon**3 to reflect thermo-mechanical interaction.
- Symmetry in tension/compression when sign is not distinguished → dependence on Abs(epsilon) instead of epsilon (isotropic magnitude-based response).
- High-temperature rapid loss of load capacity → denominators or switches dominated by exp(c*T), producing sharp decreases beyond a thermal threshold.
- Nonlinear elasticity at finite strain → inclusion of odd higher powers (epsilon**3, epsilon**5) to capture stiffening/softening without explicit kinematics.

Key structural facts:
- It is the **sum of exactly two terms**:  
  (A) \(\epsilon^{0.4776}\) times an **Arrhenius-in-\(T\)** factor \(\exp(-K/T)\) (depends on \(T\) only through \(1/T\), not linearly).

- No logs, no trig, no \(\exp(\text{const}\cdot \epsilon)\), no rational \(\epsilon/(a+|\epsilon|)\) pieces.
- Any candidate must be able (possibly after setting some coefficients to 0) to reproduce **both**: an \(\exp(-K/T)\) factor and the \(\epsilon^3(T-c)\) term.
